A provider normally\n88:  * identifies itself with a file named {@code java.security.Provider}\n89:  * in the resource directory {@code META-INF/services}.\n90:  * Security providers are looked up via the {@link ServiceLoader} mechanism\n91:  * using the {@link ClassLoader#getSystemClassLoader application class loader}.\n92:  *\n93:  * <p>Providers may be configured such that they are automatically\n94:  * installed and made available at runtime via the\n95:  * {@link Security#getProviders() Security.getProviders()} method.\n96:  * The mechanism for configuring and installing security providers is\n97:  * implementation-specific.\n98:  *\n99:  * @implNote\n100:  * The JDK implementation supports static registration of the security\n101:  * providers via the {@code conf/security/java.security} file in the Java\n102:  * installation directory. It forms the core of the Java Cryptographic\\n53:  * Extension (JCE) framework.\\n54:  *\\n55:  * <p>In order to create a {@code Cipher} object, the application calls the\\n56:  * cipher's {@code getInstance} method, and passes the name of the\\n57:  * requested <i>transformation</i> to it. Optionally, the name of a provider\\n58:  * may be specified.\\n59:  *\\n60:  * <p>A <i>transformation</i> is a string that describes the operation (or\\n61:  * set of operations) to be performed on the given input, to produce some\\n62:  * output. A transformation always includes the name of a cryptographic\\n63:  * algorithm (e.g., <i>AES</i>), and may be followed by a feedback mode and\\n64:  * padding scheme.\\n65:  *\\n66:  * <p> A transformation is of the form:\\n67:  *\\n68:  * <ul>\\n69:  * <li>\\\"<i>algorithm/mode/padding</i>\\\" or\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <li>\\\"<i>algorithm</i>\\\"\\n72:  * </ul>\\n73:  *\\n74:  * <P> (in the latter case,\\n75:  * provider-specific default values for the mode and padding scheme are used).\\n76:  * For example, the following is a valid transformation:\\n77:  *\\n78:  * <pre>\\n79:  *     Cipher c = Cipher.getInstance(\\\"<i>AES/CBC/PKCS5Padding</i>\\\");\\n80:  * </pre>\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Using modes such as {@code CFB} and {@code OFB}, block\\n83:  * ciphers can encrypt data in units smaller than the cipher's actual\\n84:  * block size.  When requesting such a mode, you may optionally specify\\n85:  * the number of bits to be processed at a time by appending this number\\n86:  * to the mode name as shown in the \\\"{@code AES/CFB8/NoPadding}\\\" and\\n87:  * \\\"{@code AES/OFB32/PKCS5Padding}\\\" transformations. If no such\\n88:  * number is specified, a provider-specific default is used.\\n89:  * (See the\\n90:  * {@extLink security_guide_jdk_providers JDK Providers Documentation}\\n91:  * for the JDK Providers default values.)\\n92:  * Thus, block ciphers can be turned into byte-oriented stream ciphers by\\n93:  * using an 8 bit mode such as CFB8 or OFB8.\\n94:  * <p>\\n95:  * Modes such as Authenticated Encryption with Associated Data (AEAD)\\n96:  * provide authenticity assurances for both confidential data and\\n97:  * Additional Associated Data (AAD) that is not encrypted.  (Please see\\n98:  * <a href=\\\"http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc5116.txt\\\"> RFC 5116 </a> for more\\n99:  * information on AEAD and AAD algorithms such as GCM/CCM.) Both\\n100:  * confidential and AAD data can be used when calculating the\\n101:  * authentication tag (similar to a {@link Mac}).  This tag is appended\\n102:  * to the ciphertext during encryption, and is verified on decryption.\\n103:  * <p>\\n104:  * AEAD modes such as GCM/CCM perform all AAD authenticity calculations\\n105:  * before starting the ciphertext authenticity calculations.  To avoid\\n106:  * implementations having to internally buffer ciphertext, all AAD data\\n107:  * must be supplied to GCM/CCM implementations (via the {@code updateAAD}\\n108:  * methods) <b>before</b> the ciphertext is processed (via\\n109:  * the {@code update} and {@code doFinal} methods).\\n110:  * <p>\\n111:  * Note that GCM mode has a uniqueness requirement on IVs used in\\n112:  * encryption with a given key. When IVs are repeated for GCM\\n113:  * encryption, such usages are subject to forgery attacks. Thus, after\\n114:  * each encryption operation using GCM mode, callers should re-initialize\\n115:  * the {@code Cipher} objects with GCM parameters which have a different IV\\n116:  * value.\\n117:  * <pre>\\n118:  *     GCMParameterSpec s = ...;\\n119:  *     cipher.init(..., s);\\n120:  *\\n121:  *     // If the GCM parameters were generated by the provider, it can\\n122:  *     // be retrieved by:\\n123:  *     // cipher.getParameters().getParameterSpec(GCMParameterSpec.class);\\n124:  *\\n125:  *     cipher.updateAAD(...);  // AAD\\n126:  *     cipher.update(...);     // Multi-part update\\n127:  *     cipher.doFinal(...);    // conclusion of operation\\n128:  *\\n129:  *     // Use a different IV value for every encryption\\n130:  *     byte[] newIv = ...;\\n131:  *     s = new GCMParameterSpec(s.getTLen(), newIv);\\n132:  *     cipher.init(..., s);\\n133:  *     ...\\n134:  *\\n135:  * </pre>\\n136:  * The ChaCha20 and ChaCha20-Poly1305 algorithms have a similar requirement\\n137:  * for unique nonces with a given key.  After each encryption or decryption\\n138:  * operation, callers should re-initialize their ChaCha20 or ChaCha20-Poly1305\\n139:  * ciphers with parameters that specify a different nonce value.  Please\\n140:  * see <a href=\\\"https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7539\\\">RFC 7539</a> for more\\n141:  * information on the ChaCha20 and ChaCha20-Poly1305 algorithms.\\n142:  * <p>\\n143:  * Every implementation of the Java platform is required to support\\n144:  * the following standard {@code Cipher} object transformations with\\n145:  * the keysizes in parentheses:\\n146:  * <ul>\\n147:  * <li>{@code AES/CBC/NoPadding} (128)</li>\\n148:  * <li>{@code AES/CBC/PKCS5Padding} (128)</li>\\n149:  * <li>{@code AES/ECB/NoPadding} (128)</li>\\n150:  * <li>{@code AES/ECB/PKCS5Padding} (128)</li>\\n151:  * <li>{@code AES/GCM/NoPadding} (128, 256)</li>\\n152:  * <li>{@code ChaCha20-Poly1305}</li>\\n153:  * <li>{@code DESede/CBC/NoPadding} (168)</li>\\n154:  * <li>{@code DESede/CBC/PKCS5Padding} (168)</li>\\n155:  * <li>{@code DESede/ECB/NoPadding} (168)</li>\\n156:  * <li>{@code DESede/ECB/PKCS5Padding} (168)</li>\\n157:  * <li>{@code RSA/ECB/PKCS1Padding} (1024, 2048)</li>\\n158:  * <li>{@code RSA/ECB/OAEPWithSHA-1AndMGF1Padding} (1024, 2048)</li>\\n159:  * <li>{@code RSA/ECB/OAEPWithSHA-256AndMGF1Padding} (1024, 2048)</li>\\n160:  * </ul>\\n161:  * These transformations are described in the\\n162:  * <a href=\\\"{@docRoot}/../specs/security/standard-names.html#cipher-algorithms\\\">\\n163:  * Cipher section</a> of the\\n164:  * Java Security Standard Algorithm Names Specification.\\n165:  * Consult the release documentation for your implementation to see if any\\n166:  * other transformations are supported.\\n167:  *\\n168:  * @spec It forms the core of the Java Cryptographic\\n53:  * Extension (JCE) framework.\\n54:  *\\n55:  * <p>In order to create a {@code Cipher} object, the application calls the\\n56:  * cipher's {@code getInstance} method, and passes the name of the\\n57:  * requested <i>transformation</i> to it. Optionally, the name of a provider\\n58:  * may be specified.\\n59:  *\\n60:  * <p>A <i>transformation</i> is a string that describes the operation (or\\n61:  * set of operations) to be performed on the given input, to produce some\\n62:  * output. A transformation always includes the name of a cryptographic\\n63:  * algorithm (e.g., <i>AES</i>), and may be followed by a feedback mode and\\n64:  * padding scheme.\\n65:  *\\n66:  * <p> A transformation is of the form:\\n67:  *\\n68:  * <ul>\\n69:  * <li>\\\"<i>algorithm/mode/padding</i>\\\" or\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <li>\\\"<i>algorithm</i>\\\"\\n72:  * </ul>\\n73:  *\\n74:  * <P> (in the latter case,\\n75:  * provider-specific default values for the mode and padding scheme are used).\\n76:  * For example, the following is a valid transformation:\\n77:  *\\n78:  * <pre>\\n79:  *     Cipher c = Cipher.getInstance(\\\"<i>AES/CBC/PKCS5Padding</i>\\\");\\n80:  * </pre>\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Using modes such as {@code CFB} and {@code OFB}, block\\n83:  * ciphers can encrypt data in units smaller than the cipher's actual\\n84:  * block size.  When requesting such a mode, you may optionally specify\\n85:  * the number of bits to be processed at a time by appending this number\\n86:  * to the mode name as shown in the \\\"{@code AES/CFB8/NoPadding}\\\" and\\n87:  * \\\"{@code AES/OFB32/PKCS5Padding}\\\" transformations. If no such\\n88:  * number is specified, a provider-specific default is used.\\n89:  * (See the\\n90:  * {@extLink security_guide_jdk_providers JDK Providers Documentation}\\n91:  * for the JDK Providers default values.)\\n92:  * Thus, block ciphers can be turned into byte-oriented stream ciphers by\\n93:  * using an 8 bit mode such as CFB8 or OFB8.\\n94:  * <p>\\n95:  * Modes such as Authenticated Encryption with Associated Data (AEAD)\\n96:  * provide authenticity assurances for both confidential data and\\n97:  * Additional Associated Data (AAD) that is not encrypted.  (Please see\\n98:  * <a href=\\\"http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc5116.txt\\\"> RFC 5116 </a> for more\\n99:  * information on AEAD and AAD algorithms such as GCM/CCM.) Both\\n100:  * confidential and AAD data can be used when calculating the\\n101:  * authentication tag (similar to a {@link Mac}).  This tag is appended\\n102:  * to the ciphertext during encryption, and is verified on decryption.\\n103:  * <p>\\n104:  * AEAD modes such as GCM/CCM perform all AAD authenticity calculations\\n105:  * before starting the ciphertext authenticity calculations.  To avoid\\n106:  * implementations having to internally buffer ciphertext, all AAD data\\n107:  * must be supplied to GCM/CCM implementations (via the {@code updateAAD}\\n108:  * methods) <b>before</b> the ciphertext is processed (via\\n109:  * the {@code update} and {@code doFinal} methods).\\n110:  * <p>\\n111:  * Note that GCM mode has a uniqueness requirement on IVs used in\\n112:  * encryption with a given key. When IVs are repeated for GCM\\n113:  * encryption, such usages are subject to forgery attacks. Thus, after\\n114:  * each encryption operation using GCM mode, callers should re-initialize\\n115:  * the {@code Cipher} objects with GCM parameters which have a different IV\\n116:  * value.\\n117:  * <pre>\\n118:  *     GCMParameterSpec s = ...;\\n119:  *     cipher.init(..., s);\\n120:  *\\n121:  *     // If the GCM parameters were generated by the provider, it can\\n122:  *     // be retrieved by:\\n123:  *     // cipher.getParameters().getParameterSpec(GCMParameterSpec.class);\\n124:  *\\n125:  *     cipher.updateAAD(...);  // AAD\\n126:  *     cipher.update(...);     // Multi-part update\\n127:  *     cipher.doFinal(...);    // conclusion of operation\\n128:  *\\n129:  *     // Use a different IV value for every encryption\\n130:  *     byte[] newIv = ...;\\n131:  *     s = new GCMParameterSpec(s.getTLen(), newIv);\\n132:  *     cipher.init(..., s);\\n133:  *     ...\\n134:  *\\n135:  * </pre>\\n136:  * The ChaCha20 and ChaCha20-Poly1305 algorithms have a similar requirement\\n137:  * for unique nonces with a given key.  After each encryption or decryption\\n138:  * operation, callers should re-initialize their ChaCha20 or ChaCha20-Poly1305\\n139:  * ciphers with parameters that specify a different nonce value.  Please\\n140:  * see <a href=\\\"https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7539\\\">RFC 7539</a> for more\\n141:  * information on the ChaCha20 and ChaCha20-Poly1305 algorithms.\\n142:  * <p>\\n143:  * Every implementation of the Java platform is required to support\\n144:  * the following standard {@code Cipher} object transformations with\\n145:  * the keysizes in parentheses:\\n146:  * <ul>\\n147:  * <li>{@code AES/CBC/NoPadding} (128)</li>\\n148:  * <li>{@code AES/CBC/PKCS5Padding} (128)</li>\\n149:  * <li>{@code AES/ECB/NoPadding} (128)</li>\\n150:  * <li>{@code AES/ECB/PKCS5Padding} (128)</li>\\n151:  * <li>{@code AES/GCM/NoPadding} (128, 256)</li>\\n152:  * <li>{@code ChaCha20-Poly1305}</li>\\n153:  * <li>{@code DESede/CBC/NoPadding} (168)</li>\\n154:  * <li>{@code DESede/CBC/PKCS5Padding} (168)</li>\\n155:  * <li>{@code DESede/ECB/NoPadding} (168)</li>\\n156:  * <li>{@code DESede/ECB/PKCS5Padding} (168)</li>\\n157:  * <li>{@code RSA/ECB/PKCS1Padding} (1024, 2048)</li>\\n158:  * <li>{@code RSA/ECB/OAEPWithSHA-1AndMGF1Padding} (1024, 2048)</li>\\n159:  * <li>{@code RSA/ECB/OAEPWithSHA-256AndMGF1Padding} (1024, 2048)</li>\\n160:  * </ul>\\n161:  * These
